  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a94c9394-4b68-4a9d-b438-8c58d026328e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer10430849472484610070">Supernatural fantasy has a new antihero in Sandman Slim, star of this gripping, gritty new series by Richard Kadrey.<br/><br/>Life sucks and then you die. Or, if you’re James Stark, you spend eleven years in Hell as a hitman before finally escaping, only to land back in the hell-on-earth that is Los Angeles.<br/><br/>Now Stark’s back, and ready for revenge. And absolution, and maybe even love</span>
  <span id="freeText10430849472484610070" style="display:none">Supernatural fantasy has a new antihero in Sandman Slim, star of this gripping, gritty new series by Richard Kadrey.<br /><br />Life sucks and then you die. Or, if you’re James Stark, you spend eleven years in Hell as a hitman before finally escaping, only to land back in the hell-on-earth that is Los Angeles.<br /><br />Now Stark’s back, and ready for revenge. And absolution, and maybe even love. But when his first stop saddles him with an abusive talking head, Stark discovers that the road to absolution and revenge is much longer than you’d expect, and both Heaven and Hell have their own ideas for his future.<br /><br />Resurrection sucks. Saving the world is worse.<br /><br />Darkly twisted, irreverent, and completely hilarious, Sandman Slim is the breakthrough novel by an acclaimed author.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/488592047?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/922495-patrick">Patrick</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/922495-patrick?shelf=books-i-would-blurb">books-i-would-blurb</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer488592047" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13629627326237470321">How could I have gone years without hearing about this book?<br/><br/>Simply said, I enjoyed it to a ridiculous degree. I picked it up mostly because of the blurbs on the back, authors I trust not to lie to me said glowing things. I was only 30 pages in when I called the local bookstore to order the other books in the series. <br/><br/>I like Kadrey's writing. It doesn't feel like he's trying desperately to impress me. It doesn't feel like he's trying to mimic the big powers in Urban Fantasy Butcher, Harris, Briggs</span>
  <span id="freeText13629627326237470321" style="display:none">How could I have gone years without hearing about this book?<br /><br />Simply said, I enjoyed it to a ridiculous degree. I picked it up mostly because of the blurbs on the back, authors I trust not to lie to me said glowing things. I was only 30 pages in when I called the local bookstore to order the other books in the series. <br /><br />I like Kadrey's writing. It doesn't feel like he's trying desperately to impress me. It doesn't feel like he's trying to mimic the big powers in Urban Fantasy Butcher, Harris, Briggs, whoever the current flavor is. Kadrey is playing his own game here, and there's a sort of "fuck you" attitude to the whole book that I really enjoyed. <br /><br />Also, the language is gorgeous. Not lyrical and arty. Kadrey has a way of phrasing things that left me smiling and chuckling to myself in public. That's a rarity for me these days.... <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13629627326237470321" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_62738572" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62738572" />
    <a title="Will Byrnes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes"><img alt="Will Byrnes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291462190p2/1526851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62738572?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will Byrnes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will Byrnes" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes">Will Byrnes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62738572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3802874405472224246">Having recently exited Hell, Stark is rather peeved at those who had sent him there for eleven years, and is eager for revenge. He has a fondness for stealing cars and making mayhem. Los Angeles comes in for some laugh-out-loud funny noir treatment.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452842601i/17749901.jpg' width='400' height='xxx' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>Richard Kadrey</b> - from his site <br/><br/>Richard Kadrey has created a world not unlike Kim Harrison’s Inderland, a blended world in which the magical and non-magical co-exist. I love Kadrey’s dark sense of humor, which reminds me very much of the <i>Hell Boy</i> serie</span>
  <span id="freeText3802874405472224246" style="display:none">Having recently exited Hell, Stark is rather peeved at those who had sent him there for eleven years, and is eager for revenge. He has a fondness for stealing cars and making mayhem. Los Angeles comes in for some laugh-out-loud funny noir treatment.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452842601i/17749901.jpg" width="400" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Richard Kadrey</b> - from his site <br><br>Richard Kadrey has created a world not unlike Kim Harrison’s Inderland, a blended world in which the magical and non-magical co-exist. I love Kadrey’s dark sense of humor, which reminds me very much of the <i>Hell Boy</i> series and Christopher Moore’s vampire books. I suppose it might be argued that <i>Sandman Slim</i> is derivative, but the weaving of magical and the real has become a staple and what counts more is how the tale is told. In <i>Sandman Slim</i> it is told very well. Kadrey maintains our interest by adding bigger-picture detail to Stark’s personal mission. There is a nice cast of supporting characters here, including a centuries old French alchemist, a spider-like person who survives by liquefying humans and drinking them, angels, anti-angels, magicians and at least one video store clerk who aspires to a bit more from life. If you thought that having one’s head cut off would be a conversation killer, think again. Kadrey has filled his stage with impressive props, magical weapons, potions, tools and pathways. This is a fast-paced fun read from start to finish. Thankfully Kadrey has kept at it and there are several more volumes if this one doesn’t leave you steaming in a very warm place.<br><br>=============================<b>EXTRA STUFF</b><br><br>Links to the author’s <a href="http://richardkadrey.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">personal</a>, <a href="https://twitter.com/Richard_Kadrey" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>, <a href="https://www.facebook.com/Richard-Kadreys-Writing-Page-172919106104575/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">FB</a> and <a href="http://kadrey.tumblr.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> pages<br><br>The Barnes and Noble Sci-Fi Fantasy Blog has a feature in which various writers tell about shows or movies that go particularly well with their novels. Kadrey's turn came up on December 1, 2016 - <a href="http://www.barnesandnoble.com/blog/sci-fi-fantasy/binge-watchers-companion-guide-richard-kadreys-everything-box-john-carpenters-apocalypse-trilogy" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">The Binge-Watcher’s Companion Guide: Richard Kadrey’s The Everything Box [his latest book] and John Carpenter’s Apocalypse Trilogy</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3802874405472224246" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18067840-sandman-slim">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Lovers of fluffy bunnies and pastel-colored rainbows</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1383542804" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11940310257461584792"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Fuck me. I’m a rock star. And all I really wanted was a burrito.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1570091585ra/28237197.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>➽ <b><u>And the moral of this reread is</u>:</b> My #1 boyfriend. <b>Worse than the bogeyman and tooth decay</b>. Not a fan of mythological soap operas (a shame, that). <b>The Joseph Stalin of laundry</b>. Loves painting walls <b>with livers and spinal cords</b>. Gives <s>fellow monsters</s> girls <b>booty calls to massacres</b>. Always in for a cigarette, a drink, <b>and a lobotomy</b>. How anyone can resist his <b>undying charm</b> is <b>one of the greatest mysteries of the univers</b></span>
  <span id="freeText11940310257461584792" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Fuck me. I’m a rock star. And all I really wanted was a burrito.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1570091585ra/28237197.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➽ <b><u>And the moral of this reread is</u>:</b> My #1 boyfriend. <b>Worse than the bogeyman and tooth decay</b>. Not a fan of mythological soap operas (a shame, that). <b>The Joseph Stalin of laundry</b>. Loves painting walls <b>with livers and spinal cords</b>. Gives <s>fellow monsters</s> girls <b>booty calls to massacres</b>. Always in for a cigarette, a drink, <b>and a lobotomy</b>. How anyone can resist his <b>undying charm</b> is <b>one of the greatest mysteries of the universe</b>, if you ask me. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <br>
  <br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587454720ra/29329610.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1554139579i/27300168._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>[<b>August 2017</b>]<br><br><b>Cunningly/shrewdly/mercilessly/whatever</b> ruling over millions of <s>mostly brain-dead</s> murderous crustaceans doesn't mean one cannot be a complete, utter idiot <s>sometimes</s>. I mean, look at this <b>delicious little piece of uproariously gruesome beauty</b> here. It's been sitting unread on my <s>to-be-ruthlessly-crushed</s> to-be-read shelf for <b>TWO bloody shrimping years</b>. You really have to be <s>some special kind of nitwit</s> a little distracted to let such a <b>disgraceful, revolting thing</b> happen. In my defense, I have to say that my rampaging, decapodic kids are forever and always getting mixed up in subaquatic skirmishes, so it's no wonder I end up missing out on some <b>slightly scrumptious</b> books sometimes. Ergo, I forgive myself. Such a <b>splendidly generous</b> soul I am <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504088392ra/23723828.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><br><b>So. Why should I have read this decades, if not centuries ago, you ask? Because</b>:<br><br>➽ <b>This world. This story</b>. It's original. It's creative. It's dark and noir and stuff. It's gritty. It's messy. It's blackly hilarious. It's twisted. It's brutal. <b>It's quite devastatingly beautiful, really</b>. Also, it features asshole angels and yummy demons. And <b>bloody shrimping Lucifer</b> (aka my hero and role-model extraordinaire) himself. You just cannot go wrong with such a beautiful collection of <b>cunning, devious, ruthless, perverse, murderous bastards</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587454720ra/29329611.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➽ <b>This writing</b>. It's first person, present tense (and I <s> loved</s> <b>slightly liked</b> it anyway *utters a shrimpy gasp*). It's scrumptiously <b>in-your-face</b> and charmingly aggressive. It's non-stop <s>bloodbath</s> <b>action</b>. And it's one hell <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>pun somewhat intended. You are quite welcome</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> of a <b>page-turner</b> despite the weird book structure (or lack thereof and stuff). Think of it as a perpetual <s>acid high</s> <b>adrenaline rush</b> that will keep kicking you in the <s>lovely</s> derrière until your turn the <b>very last page</b>. Which is kind of <b>scrumptious</b> and stuff. <br><br>➽ <b>This Jimmy Stark/Just Stark/Sandman Slim/New boyfriend of mine</b>. He is a teensy little bit <s>fucked-up</s> <s>screwed-up</s> <b>messed-up</b> after spending the last 11 years of his life in Hell (fun times). He is delectably <b>raw</b>. He is exquisitely <s>offensive</s> <s>foul-mouthed</s> <s>irreverent</s> <b>rude</b>. And wickedly <b>snarky</b>, too. Also, he shoots/cuts/chops first and asks questions later. His <b>slightly</b> violent tendencies really are a thing of beauty. I like to think of him as my boyfriend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/131794-daniel-faust" rel="nofollow noopener">Daniel Faust's</a> <b>somewhat demented/manic/homicidal/vindictive cousin</b> from L.A. So much bloody shrimping <b>hotness</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489018812ra/22178149.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>No wonder</b> it was <s>lust</s> love at first sight between us. I mean, how was I supposed to NOT fall for him, when he says <b>lovely, delicate stuff</b> like: <i>"If either of these guys even blinks funny, I’m going to be <b>painting the walls with livers and spinal cords</b>."</i> And, just like that, <b>forever doomed I was</b>. Yes, it is quite official: <b>I am in LURVE</b> <s>again</s> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>warning: the following spoiler might hurt the sensitivity of some barnacles</i>
  <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[❤❤❤❤❤❤❤❤❤❤❤❤❤<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>EW EW EW</b> and <b>YUCK YUCK YUCK</b> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br><br>➽ <b>This yummy cast of luscious supporting characters</b>. Such a beautiful collection of benevolent, sane, gentle, decent, sophisticated personas here. And it's not only the <s>the villainous villains</s> <b>well-meaning Mother Theresa wannabes</b> I am talking about here. I mean, they are quite adoption-worthy in a pleasingly repulsive way, but it's my Stark's sidekicks I have a <b>perverted weakness</b> for: <b>Vidocq</b> because, you know, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eug%C3%A8ne_Fran%C3%A7ois_Vidocq" rel="nofollow noopener">Vidocq</a> and stuff. <b>Kasabian</b>, because, who would not fall for a sleazy, obnoxious undead head? And <b>I am SO Kidnapping You Candy the Jade</b> (IaSKYCtJ™), because: <i>"Candy isn’t using the guns anymore. She’s back to teeth and claws, <b>a meat grinder in tight jeans and Chuck Taylors</b>."</i> So beautiful. <b>Sigh</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504085597ra/23723615.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Cute, caring, affectionate teddy bears really are pretty disgusting, if you ask me.</i><br><br>» And the moral of this <b>If You Are a Fan of Historical Romances and Cute Love Stories then this is THE Book for You Crappy Non Review</b> (IYAaFoHRaCLSttiTBfYCNR™) is: this is so bloody shrimping good I am going to jump straight into book 2. When I should be <b>somewhat devouring</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35672796-edge-of-forever" rel="nofollow noopener">Edge of Forever</a>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504081987ra/23723307.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Yeah yeah yeah, shame on me and all that crap</b>, but I have Awesome Pippa DaCosta's blessing and stuff, <b>so there</b>.<br><br>· <b>Book 2</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1815111467" rel="nofollow noopener">Kill the Dead</a> ★★★★★<br>· <b>Book 3</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2107256238" rel="nofollow noopener">Aloha from Hell</a> ★★★★<br>· <b>Book 3.5</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2118668582" rel="nofollow noopener">Devil in the Dollhouse</a> ★★★★★<br>· <b>Book 4</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2118668627" rel="nofollow noopener">Devil Said Bang</a> ★★★★<br>· <b>Book 5</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2140195171" rel="nofollow noopener">Kill City Blues</a> ★★★★<br>· <b>Book 6</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2140195421" rel="nofollow noopener">The Getaway God</a> ★★★★★<br>· <b>Book 7</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2140195583" rel="nofollow noopener">Killing Pretty</a> ★★★★<br>· <b>Book 8</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2140195855" rel="nofollow noopener">The Perdition Score</a> ★★★★★<br>· <b>Book 9</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2140196029" rel="nofollow noopener">The Kill Society</a> ★★★★★<br>· <b>Book 10</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2259923971" rel="nofollow noopener">Hollywood Dead</a> ★★★★★<br>· <b>Book 11</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3040365658" rel="nofollow noopener">Ballistic Kiss</a> - <i>to be read</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479540926i/21203689._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>[<b>Pre-review nonsense</b>]<br><br><b>
  <u>Sandman Slim</u>
</b>. Slightly <b>unhinged</b>. Slightly <b>screwed up</b>. Slightly <b>reckless</b>. Slightly <b>violent</b>. Slightly <b>enraged</b>. Slightly <b>hilarious</b> in a beautifully <b>offensive</b> way. Out for delicious <b>revenge</b>. Just my kind of prince: <b>not bloody shrimping charming at all</b>.<br><br><b>BOOM</b>.<br><br><b>Kidnapped</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1540889681ra/26519818.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>» Full <b>Jimmy I Lurves Him Stark Just Made it Directly to the Most Scrumptious Boyfriends Ever High Security Wing of my High Security Harem YUM and Stuff Super Crappy Non Review</b> (JILHSJMiDttMSBEHSWomHSHYaDSCNR) to come.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_97394766" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97394766" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97394766?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=dark-and-gritty">dark-and-gritty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=hardboiled-and-noir">hardboiled-and-noir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=2006-2010">2006-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=angels-demons-heaven-hell">angels-demons-heaven-hell</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97394766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2693165728093097558"><b>WOWZA!!</b> Rarely have I encountered a main character so loaded with <b>ANGSTY RAGENESS</b> and <b>OMNIDIRECTIONAL BADITUDE</b> as James Stark (aka Sandman Slim). I mean this guy is full of <b> ARRRRRRRRRRGGGGHHHH!</b>...and it works...mostly. <br/><br/>Now let me say at the outset that I don’t read a ton of Keith Urban Fantasy. I enjoy <i>The Dresden Files</i> on a casual, non-rabid, basis and despite wanting to bitch-slap the main character for his all too often bouts of annoying. I really liked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/663098.The_Devil_You_Know__Felix_Castor___1_' title='The Devil You Know (Felix Castor, #1) by Mike Carey' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Devil You Know</a> and plan on reading</span>
  <span id="freeText2693165728093097558" style="display:none"><b>WOWZA!!</b> Rarely have I encountered a main character so loaded with <b>ANGSTY RAGENESS</b> and <b>OMNIDIRECTIONAL BADITUDE</b> as James Stark (aka Sandman Slim). I mean this guy is full of <b> ARRRRRRRRRRGGGGHHHH!</b>...and it works...mostly. <br /><br />Now let me say at the outset that I don’t read a ton of Keith Urban Fantasy. I enjoy <i>The Dresden Files</i> on a casual, non-rabid, basis and despite wanting to bitch-slap the main character for his all too often bouts of annoying. I really liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/663098.The_Devil_You_Know__Felix_Castor___1_" title="The Devil You Know (Felix Castor, #1) by Mike Carey" rel="nofollow noopener">The Devil You Know</a> and plan on reading more of that series and I am absolutely <b>Cocoa Puff Coo Coo</b> for the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2570856.Monster_Hunter_International__MHI___1_" title="Monster Hunter International (MHI, #1) by Larry Correia" rel="nofollow noopener">Monster Hunter International</a> series. <br /><br />To that rather scrawny list, I now add the Sandman Slim series which I plan to continue reading as I think it has serious upside potential. Here’s the skinny:<br /><br />In a world where magic and supernatural creatures are known to exist, Stark was a powerful magician in love with the only woman who ever really accepted him for who he was. Life was sitting pretty...until Stark was betrayed by a group of his magician “friends” who had him literally sent to Hell in exchange for power, wealth and other assorted knick knacks. Oh, and the magic-wielding <b>chunk-o-turds</b> also decided to go ahead and kill the love of his life. Can anyone else see the rage clouds of the revenge storm beginning to form? <br /><br />Flashforward 11 years later….<br /><br />Stark is back from Hell and the experience seems to have been pretty handy. He’s not only survived but managed to pick up some new skills (including virtual invulnerability), a few demon-built <b>go go gadgets</b> and increased his overall badassery quotient exponentially. To make matters worse for the <b>assbaskets</b> that betrayed him, his pissed off meter has also undergone a round of steroid therapy and is glued on red. Stark is back from Hell for revenge on the six who sent him there, especially the head of the group named Mason himself has become mega powerful thanks to arranging Stark's little tour of Hell. <br /><br />This is the UF genre’s take on hardcore noir fiction. Stark is a <b>paranormalfied</b> version of your typical noirtastic main character. In fact, Stark’s name and the fact that one of the main bad guys is named Parker are pretty clear homage to noir fiction giant, Donald Westlake and his Parker novels (which he wrote under the name Stark).<br /><br />I liked the world-building and Stark's revenge quest has him bumping into all kinds of <i>bump in the night</i> baddies as well as Nazi skin heads with demonic weaponry, and a team from Homeland Security sporting soem serious angelic firepower. <br /><br />There are no real good guys in the cosmic battle ground and ever the angels are played with huge streaks of gray in them. Stark has nothing but contempt for both sides and treats them all with a hearty “fuck yourself” as he sees them as two sides of the same crooked coin. I liked Stark's <i>"you can kill me but you can't control me and I promise you'll limp when its over"</i> mindset. <br /><br />This is espcially true when dealing with the "good" angels who he holds in special contempt. His anger lacede, expletive topped tirades at what they and their Boss have allowed to happen on Earth are some of the best moments in the book. Dark yes, blasphemous, oh yeah...but seriously compelling reading. <br /><br />In the end, I liked Stark and the fact that he never really mellowed during the book. You are in his head throughout the book and so you know he is not really “evil” and so it is easy to like the guy. He has a moral code (if seriously jaded and rough around the edges) and he looks out for his friends. It did take me a while to warm-up to him as he spent way to much time telegraphing his dumb mistakes and vacationing in the land of self-pity that the he seemed to be spiraling down to <b>doucheville</b>. However, he recovered nicely and when it finally came down to knocking heads around, he was a one man force of nature that was pure fun to watch. <br /><br />By the end of the book I was sold on Stark's potential as a really good character. His inner monologues and outer tirades were often spiced with heavy doses of funny and I liked the overall tone of the story. The writing was good and certainly didn’t detract from the story-telling. <br /><br />3.5 stars for this one and high hopes for future installments. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2693165728093097558" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_68805779" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/68805779" />
    <a title="Kemper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/405390-kemper"><img alt="Kemper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495476851p2/405390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/68805779?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kemper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kemper" href="/user/show/405390-kemper">Kemper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer68805779" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7861904326426632432">Ever read a book and find yourself thinking, "This is pretty good, but it could have been face-melting awesome."? This is one of those books for me. I really liked it, but found myself picking some serious nits while reading it.<br/><br/>Stark was a magician (a real magician, not a sawing-a-woman-in-half kind) who was madly in love with his girlfriend Alice when he was betrayed by another magician named Mason and some others. Mason managed to send Stark to hell, but as a living person, not a dead soul. <br/><br/>11</span>
  <span id="freeText7861904326426632432" style="display:none">Ever read a book and find yourself thinking, "This is pretty good, but it could have been face-melting awesome."? This is one of those books for me. I really liked it, but found myself picking some serious nits while reading it.<br /><br />Stark was a magician (a real magician, not a sawing-a-woman-in-half kind) who was madly in love with his girlfriend Alice when he was betrayed by another magician named Mason and some others. Mason managed to send Stark to hell, but as a living person, not a dead soul. <br /><br />11 years later, Stark learns that Alice has been murdered on Earth by Mason and his pals. Determined to get revenge, Stark breaks out of hell with a magical key that allows him to access almost any point in any dimension. His stay in hell has made him supernaturally tough with an extremely bad attitude, but he soon runs across various angels, demons, monsters, alchemists, magicians, Nazi skin-heads and porn shop owners that he has to deal with as he learns that there may be something much bigger than his revenge at stake.<br /><br />This had a great concept with a lot of original ideas and some terrific action. Mixing magic with various weapons, including shotguns, makes for some awesome carnage when thing really get rolling.<br /><br />However, for the first 250 pages or so, Stark just comes across as an unlikeable asshole who blunders about warning his enemies he's back and generally getting his ass kicked. (I've noticed a common factor among supernatural characters like Harry Dresden or Joe Pitt that three-quarters of the books seem to consist of them getting beaten to a pulp by various beasties and this book continues that trend.) The first half of this book consists mainly of Stark complaining about all the clothes he's ruined by getting repeatedly abused.<br /><br />The author has a bad habit of having Stark do stupid things, that he acknowledges as stupid, just to advance the plot and it's just chalked up to him being 'impulsive'. Plus, there are some serious logic gaps. Stark can access any point in any dimesion with his supernatural key. Yet, he seems to prefer stealing cars. And when he needs to dispose of a body, he steals yet another car and thinks about how many chances he's taking as he drops the body in the La Brea tar pits. Why wouldn't he just use the key and take the body to Antartica or the middle of the Amazon and just dump it? It doesn't help that he uses the key about 5 seconds after dumping the body.<br /><br />However, the ending redeemed this book a lot. When the action finally starts, it gets massive in scale and imaginative in how weapons and magic could be blended. Stark become a bad-ass anti-hero instead of a whining jerk, and the ending sets up a lot of possibilities. I hope future ones are more like the second half of the book and less like the first half.<br /><br />Oh, and for you Donald Westlake fans, the main character's name is Stark and one of the bad guys is named Parker. Get it?<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7861904326426632432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2281666583" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2281666583" />
    <a title="Orient" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43587353-orient"><img alt="Orient" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500791761p2/43587353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2281666583?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Orient" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Orient" href="/user/show/43587353-orient">Orient</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780061999444" href="/book/show/7598206-sandman-slim">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=bloody-romance">bloody-romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2281666583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15945139995265187336"> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1518677738i/25063153.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>Ohhh, "Sandman Slim", what a date it was! My first encounter with dear Mr. Stark aka lovely Sandman Slim was when I read the great reviews of Sarah, the Murderous 💜 I was deeply charmed and intrigued, well mostly because my latest date with Daniel Faust wasn’t very gripping for me and I was looking for another great character (with some similar abilities) in the lead to woot, drool and swoon for! And I found him for sure in "Sandman Slim" 💜<br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518677738ra/25063154.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Interesting plot with great action, blood, gore and mi</b></span>
  <span id="freeText15945139995265187336" style="display:none"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1518677738i/25063153.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Ohhh, "Sandman Slim", what a date it was! My first encounter with dear Mr. Stark aka lovely Sandman Slim was when I read the great reviews of Sarah, the Murderous 💜 I was deeply charmed and intrigued, well mostly because my latest date with Daniel Faust wasn’t very gripping for me and I was looking for another great character (with some similar abilities) in the lead to woot, drool and swoon for! And I found him for sure in "Sandman Slim" 💜<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518677738ra/25063154.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Interesting plot with great action, blood, gore and mindblowing humor (more with dark spices which I totally loved).</b><br><br>“Sandman Slim” is cleverly entwined, packed with fast pace and humor rollercoaster. The story is spiced with comical scenes, sarcastic sneak peeks into pop culture and ordinary life. All this is flanked with lots of action scenes, hitman stuff, moral issues, and mythological god vs devil fight. Some scenes may make you flinch if the removal if various body parts, lots of blood, gore and violence is not your everyday read! I like it in my fantasy reads so “Sandman Slim” reading experience was like watching a great thriller on TV.<br><br>I fell in love with this book for its smart, kick-ass humor, it serves well as a counterweight to the darker violent side and makes this a subtle, gripping and enjoyable read.<br><br> <b>
  <i>.“Suit yourself. But with magic, I don’t ever run out of ammo.”<br>“No, just brains.”</i>
</b><br><br> <b>
  <i>Word must have gotten around about my cage match with M…. and the K…...<br>F*ck me. I’m a rock star. And all I really wanted was a burrito.</i>
</b><br><br><br><b>Memorable characters I can fangirl for.</b><br><br>My fave part! Let the swooning begin 😆💜 There’s so much I love in Mr. Stark! He’s is a hard-core, self-concious, witty anti-hero. He knows what real hell is and he feels sorrow and pain like all of us, and he fights RL kicking and screaming! His roots, his past, wow. But that doesn’t make him a grumpy misery person. He’s the same awesome or even more than Dirty Harry! Broadcasting dark humor in Jack Daniels style, fighting the world with wonderful magic makes him a perfect anti-hero for me.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518677738ra/25063155.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>
  <i>But I didn’t die.<br>I don’t know if it was the spells, the drugs, the Aqua Regia, or just clean living, but I was changing. Every time I should have died but didn’t, I got stronger. That meant that the next attack had to be harder, faster, even more ferocious than the one before. After a while, I actually looked forward to the beat-downs. Each one changed me and that change meant that I was immune from a similar attack next time. By the end, I was a flesh-and-bone, armor-plated Dirty Harry.</i>
</b><br><br> <b>
  <i>“What the hell is wrong with your clothes?”<br>“Yeah. I had a little accident coming into town,” I say, giving her a sheepish grin. It’s a look that girls used to like when I was young and not entirely unhandsome. Talking to a cute human girl that I might have flirted with in my former life, I forget for a second that I’m no longer young or handsome. I shift to what I hope was a more neutral expression.<br>“I might need to pick up some new things. What do you think?”<br>“Don’t bother. I hear that arson is the new black.”</i>
</b><br><br> <b>
  <i>“Aw. Dying didn’t work out for you? Boo hoo. Shove your James Dean wet dreams up your ass. At the end of the day, you’re still Sandman Slim and I’m still a head in a bag that smells like someone used it to store an extra ass.”<br>“I miss Alice.”<br>“I miss my balls.” K……….. looks around. “Who f*cked up my room?”<br>“It’s my room now and you did. When you blew yourself up.”<br>“Oh, right. That sucked.”</i>
</b> Aww, sweet K 💜😆<br><br>Wanna know about the baddies in this book? Damn it, but there are lots of them! I can literally count goodies on one hand fingers. While there are hundreds of twisted, cruel, perfect villains lurking there to entertain you 😱💜 <br><br> <b>
  <i>?”If Donald Trump and the Wicked Witch of the West had a kid, it would be J……. She looks like a librarian with some money and good taste in clothes, but underneath the Versace, she’s Godzilla with tits…”</i>
</b><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1518677738i/25063156.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Magical creatures and magical world in total.</b><br><br>I enjoyed the magical system and creatures in this book. If it was my ordinary fantasy read, I would have found some common plot with demons and magic (You know it: There lived a nice guy with sh*tty past and RL, he did some magic and saved the world from some demons or/and monsters. Voila!), but thanks god (or devil? 😆) it wasn’t. I enjoyed the sneak peeks into magical world with master magicians and various evil creatures like fallen (or not) angels, devils, jades. The magical weapons and things did get me excited for real (now I know what I want for this Christmas!)<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447915923ra/17068146.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518677738ra/25063157.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518677738ra/25063158.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b><i>He changed, right in front of us. His skin, his bones, his whole body turned weird. It kind of glowed and it looked like there were things crawling around under his skin.”<br>“Sounds like they gave him an assload of nebiros.”<br>“What’s a nebiro?”<br>“A parasite. They live off the energy of whatever they infest. The only reason the host doesn’t drop dead immediately is that the nebiros excrete supernatural energy. They shit magic. It supercharges the host, keeping him and the parasite alive…”</i></b><br><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518677738ra/25063159.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><br> To sum up, ”Sandman Slim” is a gripping revenge story that caught me in its witty embrace and didn’t let go even after finishing the book. <br><br>💜 The characters are fascinating and likable even with their dark screwed-up side.<br>💜The action, humor and magic packed story is well-written and gripping. <br><br>This book is awesome and I’ll be most happy to continue my playdate with Mr. Stark 💜💜💜<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1518677738i/25063160._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>P.S. There is gonna be Sandman Slim on the screen!!!!!<br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.slashfilm.com/sandman-slim-movie-chad-stahelski/">http://www.slashfilm.com/sandman-slim...</a><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15844842123239515750">*** 4.25 ***<br/><br/><br/>"I'm hard on things. Everything ends up broken, ripped apart, modified, stuck together or shot to shit. I'd be naked as Adam and cold as a polar bear if it weren't for duct tape."<br/><br/>A gritty, unapologetic, demonic Pulp Fiction! What a fun read! Not for the tender hearted nor the young, but for all of us who are fans of episodic serial pulp-noir, full of raw prose and very little which indicates the book and the author take themselves too seriously, this is right up our alley. <br/><br/>A young hu</span>
  <span id="freeText15844842123239515750" style="display:none">*** 4.25 ***<br /><br /><br />"I'm hard on things. Everything ends up broken, ripped apart, modified, stuck together or shot to shit. I'd be naked as Adam and cold as a polar bear if it weren't for duct tape."<br /><br />A gritty, unapologetic, demonic Pulp Fiction! What a fun read! Not for the tender hearted nor the young, but for all of us who are fans of episodic serial pulp-noir, full of raw prose and very little which indicates the book and the author take themselves too seriously, this is right up our alley. <br /><br />A young human magician is thrown by some "friends" into Hell and he returns back to LA 11 years later ready for some payback. It is violent, graphic, hilarious and full of very quotable sayings, but if I try to put more of them here, it will take my whole evening... There be monsters, there be Angels, there be shady and vile humans... There is enough blood being spilled to satisfy a starving vampire... Add a very angry, lost, and if it was his choice, constantly heavily inebriated serial killer with no social skills, and you get the picture. If this sounds like something you might like, I will strongly recommend it! This is my first read and I am sure I will be tackling the complete rest of the series! Let's find out who will rule the world - Heaven, Hell or the few adventurous and very corrupt humans and fallen angels... I am rooting for ... not sure yet:):):) Shell we find out?:) <br /><br /><br />"I'm going to kill some people," I tell him. I pour the Jack into the coffee. "Probably a lot of people."<br />The bartender picks up a rag and starts wiping glasses. "Guess someone's got to."<br />"Thanks for understanding."<br /><br /><br />Now I wish you all Happy Reading and many more wonderful books to come!!!</span>

<div id="review_165143105" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/165143105" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/165143105?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to carol.  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/8476972-kristen">Kristen</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=male-lead">male-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer165143105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7349085585567045602">After the second read-through, I've come to the conclusion that <u>Sandman Slim</u> is Jason Statham starring in a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/41942.Simon_R__Green' title='Simon R. Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>Simon R. Green</a> Nightside story. Pulpy urban fantasy on steroids, it's perfect for an adrenalin read, but I recommend a pass if you are in the mood for deep thinking or don't feel up for violence.<br/><br/>Jason-cough- I mean, Stark--has made it out of Hell and is looking for revenge. Eleven years ago, six fellow members of a magic circle sent him to Hell, and his mission is to kill them all. Landing</span>
  <span id="freeText7349085585567045602" style="display:none">After the second read-through, I've come to the conclusion that <u>Sandman Slim</u> is Jason Statham starring in a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/41942.Simon_R__Green" title="Simon R. Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Simon R. Green</a> Nightside story. Pulpy urban fantasy on steroids, it's perfect for an adrenalin read, but I recommend a pass if you are in the mood for deep thinking or don't feel up for violence.<br /><br />Jason-cough- I mean, Stark--has made it out of Hell and is looking for revenge. Eleven years ago, six fellow members of a magic circle sent him to Hell, and his mission is to kill them all. Landing in a Hollywood cemetery, he quickly robs a suit and steals a car. After stopping at the Bamboo House of Dolls bar for a drink, he finds Kasabian, circle scapegoat, running a porn shop on the Hollywood strip. He meets Kas' manager, Allegra; goes on a shopping trip for new leathers and boots; and stops at his old apartment where he finds Vidocq, an alchemist, a thief and an old friend. Money is an issue if he's going to complete his goals (isn't it always?), so Vidocq hooks him up with a storekeeper that needs an odd job or two done.<br /><br />I read voraciously until about a third in, when it became more of a struggle. Somehow, that seems backwards. There were several interesting ideas that elevated it above the mundane, including Stark's acquired resistance to injury, the Jade and the underlying celestial conflict. I found the Jade especially enjoyable, her Chuck Taylors and their 'first date' together. While the Sub Rosa was a snooze, the Inquisitor Medea was nicely described and menacing. Somewhat dreading a stereotypical war of heaven versus hell, I enjoyed Kadrey's solution to the traditional plotting dualism. The ending had a great plot twist that surprised me.<br /><br />More troublesome was the middle of the road creativity, largely of the kitchen sink variety. I think my eyes rolled about the time the Nazis showed up to toss the bar. I know they did when there was a trip to the magic emporium, and by the time the Men in Black appeared, I'm sure I looked possessed. Then the dialogue had loads of one liners made for action movies, with far too many cultural references. Brad Pitt? Scarface? <i>Two</i> Donald Trump references? <i>Suuuure,</i> eleven years in Hell. Sure, the devil steals cable.<br /><br />A number of inexplicably odd tactical moves and inconsistencies left me wondering if Stark was supposed to be dumb, or the plotting was just that underdeveloped. Yes, I know I'm talking about logic in a book about a man who escaped Hell. But the general idea of a fantasy/sci-fi book is that the logic of the world and the characters needs to be consistent. Since the world basically was, I was left with the conclusion that the protag wasn't heavy on the thinking skills. One minute concerned about exposure, the next minute not <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(inviting the store manager into the fold?). <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> One minute making a deal about having a job (albeit owning a porn shop), the next minute not (blood on the floor? Paying the stoner help?). Decides he's fine without his friends then <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ drops/risks everything to help them  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Then the hero is a bit of a Mary Sue fighter--talented, invincible between his physical fighting skills, his damage proofing and his magic key. But oh-so-dumb. Not my favorite kind of hero.<br /><br />There is a lot of violent imagery here. Not that there are violent scenes--which there are, but usually not gore-focused--but our hero also fantasizes about violence. But his is the good clean, funny variety, while the bad guys go for real evil.<br /><br />Overall--enjoyable, definitely a fast read. Doesn't seem to be taking itself too seriously, so for the right reading mindset, it's a nice bit of fun. I'll try the next just to see where several interesting shiny bits might lead, and maybe to answer the question where the Sandman Slim label comes in.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="7349085585567045602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_113110719" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/113110719" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/113110719?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113110719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7458064719754319577">I guess I'm just getting old, but I'm so tired. I started 3 (4 if you count Tooth Fairy which I gave all of 2 stars) Urban Fantasies recently...one I took off my books completely as a waste of time and I didn't even bother to rate or review it...another I stopped reading and gave 1 star as another in a long line of anti-hero clones etc...now this one, and it's the same. I don't mind antiheroes, if their good antiheroes. This is another mouthy guy with attitude that I can't find even remotely bel</span>
  <span id="freeText7458064719754319577" style="display:none">I guess I'm just getting old, but I'm so tired. I started 3 (4 if you count Tooth Fairy which I gave all of 2 stars) Urban Fantasies recently...one I took off my books completely as a waste of time and I didn't even bother to rate or review it...another I stopped reading and gave 1 star as another in a long line of anti-hero clones etc...now this one, and it's the same. I don't mind antiheroes, if their good antiheroes. This is another mouthy guy with attitude that I can't find even remotely believable, in a world where "good is rejected and Satan is seen (again) as a fairly reasonable guy. (Heaven and hell are pretty much the same, attitude wise apparently. I mean he has hell, so I guess he had to have "a heaven"). The "protagonist" opens the book having sneaked out of hell apparently having learned nothing from the experience. I mean hell seems to be pretty much pointless. The first thing the guy informs us is that he hates cops and hero types...but sometimes he has to intervene and do the "right thing". He's explaining why he intervened in a brutal carjacking...shameful for any tough, mouthy, antihero. I just couldn't get involved with this guy or his story.<br /><br />Maybe I'm too old and have read too much of this crap...but enjoy it if you like. I find it just what I called it above.<br /><br />There are very, very good urban fantasies out there. It's just too bad they seem to be hard to find. Or maybe I'm just too critical or particular...still, I love some Urban Fantasy books, some are pretty good, some just okay and others I find I wish I hadn't put my time into. If you think it's cool to sneer at life, embrace nihilism, and determine what's right and wrong by your own appetites, enjoy. Not for me. I'm frankly tired of idealization of protagonists who are "cool" because they "get away with it", or however you want to state it.Third loser book in a row and I guess I'm a little tired (have I told you that?). Hope I can find a brain candy book next that I enjoy reading. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7458064719754319577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2077526046" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2077526046" />
    <a title="mark monday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday"><img alt="mark monday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572672245p2/131922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2077526046?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mark monday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mark monday" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday">mark monday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=secret-histories">secret-histories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2077526046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11377205873459953425">mean magician Sandman Slim returns from Hell to smash, slash, burn, beat, maim, and kill. it appears his time spent in the lower depth's gladiator arenas has only served to sharpen his skills rather than to mellow his temper. fortunately, he's not a bad guy and he's exercising his violent capabilities in Los Angeles, where there is plenty of room (and need) for such endeavors. he's an endearing sort - a man on a mission with a heart of gold. well maybe not gold, but certainly high quality silver</span>
  <span id="freeText11377205873459953425" style="display:none">mean magician Sandman Slim returns from Hell to smash, slash, burn, beat, maim, and kill. it appears his time spent in the lower depth's gladiator arenas has only served to sharpen his skills rather than to mellow his temper. fortunately, he's not a bad guy and he's exercising his violent capabilities in Los Angeles, where there is plenty of room (and need) for such endeavors. he's an endearing sort - a man on a mission with a heart of gold. well maybe not gold, but certainly high quality silver at least.<br /><br />the book is endearing as well. Kadrey tries to come across all hard-boiled but the book reads as if the author was just as addicted to Buffy the Vampire Slayer and Angel as I was. straightforward writing with snarky, snappy dialogue that is often so on the nose that it made me wince, but also often a lot of breezy fun. there's much rushing back and forth and appearing in places suddenly (yay, magic) and swift reversals of fortune and just as swift reclamations of fortune; Kadrey keeps the pace popping but makes sure the story remains clear and the mysteries remain intriguing and engaging. I particularly enjoyed our hero's angst and irritation over his limited clothing options because I often feel similarly, although not usually because my clothes have been bloodied and burnt due to slaughtering various enemies (only sometimes). I also quite liked that talking head named Kasabian; possibly because I also like the band Kasabian. overall the book is a light delight and quite easy going down. fans of Urban Fantasy probably have already read this; if not, they should be reading this series as soon as possible.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11377205873459953425" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-urban">fantasy-urban</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1370089316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17497741956726144791">Finally finished this and I would have sooner but I'm such a slave to my Kindle and had this in paperback.   <span id="freeText17497741956726144791" style="display:none">Finally finished this and I would have sooner but I'm such a slave to my Kindle and had this in paperback. James Stark (Jimmy/Sandman Slim) is back from Hell and out for vengeance. He is going to murder the dark magicians who killed him and the love of his life. If only she had been as hard to kill as he was.<br><br>Being back in LA takes some getting used to and Jimmy meets new friends and reunites with old ones. There are some racist skinheads, a recovering vampire addict (Candy is awesome, but she had to give up drinking blood from the source because going vamp in this world means you pretty much go psycho and Candy would rather not lose herself in blood lust). <br><br>Allegra is the chick who works at Maximum Overdrive (video rental/porn store). Vidocq is the bad-ass magician who takes her on as an apprentice and is one of Jimmy's old friends. Kinski is the doctor who whips up Candy's vampire shakes and performs magical surgeries.<br><br>Throw in a lot of demons, including Satan himself, some semi-angel/demons who feed off fear, some actual angels, and a secret government-type group helping the angels, and this is a darkly funny, entertaining urban fantasy that is extremely well-written, sarcastic, and even a little nostalgic. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534785334i/26165137.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Buddy read with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148935-dust-off-your-machalo-it-s-time-for-another-buddy-read" rel="nofollow noopener">MacHalos</a>. New book and bookmark from B&amp;N. #BirthdaySplurge :))</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16700305722731391682">Okay, this is NOT a children’s book, just FYI. This is noir urban fantasy, like Jim Butcher’s Harry Dresden series, but even grittier. The main character, James Stark, aka Sandman Slim, is betrayed by a group of powerful magicians and dragged bodily into Hell, where he spends eleven years fighting in the gladiator pits of Lucifer. Somehow he survives, and eventually manages to escape back to Los Angeles. Now he’s looking for the people who betrayed him, but to get revenge, he’ll have to navigate</span>
  <span id="freeText16700305722731391682" style="display:none">Okay, this is NOT a children’s book, just FYI. This is noir urban fantasy, like Jim Butcher’s Harry Dresden series, but even grittier. The main character, James Stark, aka Sandman Slim, is betrayed by a group of powerful magicians and dragged bodily into Hell, where he spends eleven years fighting in the gladiator pits of Lucifer. Somehow he survives, and eventually manages to escape back to Los Angeles. Now he’s looking for the people who betrayed him, but to get revenge, he’ll have to navigate a world of angels, demons, vampires, magicians, and plenty of ruthless mortals with lots of secrets to hide. This is a rock ‘em sock ‘em adventure narrated in fresh, crackling hardboiled prose, with plenty of dark humor. I liked it so much I immediately bought the sequel, Kill the Dead. But again, this is very adult stuff. Not a YA fantasy.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4624887626083843384">So I just read this and now I have a big problem. I just want to go, "squeeeee squeeeee squeeeee" about the book, raving like a lunatic about how much I loved it, about how I had just found my next favorite UF series, but that doesn't actually SAY anything, you know?<br/><br/>But you know UFs. It's ALL about voice. The snark-meter is dinging all the time in this one. <br/><br/>I'm totally enjoying the fish-out-of-water vibe, too, but more than all the rest, it's like we got a grown-up, jaded Hogwarts alumni who had</span>
  <span id="freeText4624887626083843384" style="display:none">So I just read this and now I have a big problem. I just want to go, "squeeeee squeeeee squeeeee" about the book, raving like a lunatic about how much I loved it, about how I had just found my next favorite UF series, but that doesn't actually SAY anything, you know?<br /><br />But you know UFs. It's ALL about voice. The snark-meter is dinging all the time in this one. <br /><br />I'm totally enjoying the fish-out-of-water vibe, too, but more than all the rest, it's like we got a grown-up, jaded Hogwarts alumni who had been sold out by his friends to Hell, was given special *refining* attentions in Hell's gladiator pits, and then eventually found his way back to Earth, 11 years later, to get a little payback. <br /><br />Noir magic, folks. No side is on the side of the angels, even the angels. And everyone has an angle. The name is survival on the streets, ya'll, and Sandman Slim FITS with Los Angeles. All these elements are fantastic, but it's how Kadrey puts them together and tops it with a great voice that makes this sing.<br /><br />Am I going to binge-read these?<br /><br />MAYBE. :) <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_978725684" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/978725684" />
    <a title="Robert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5537205-robert"><img alt="Robert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505620458p2/5537205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/978725684?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert" href="/user/show/5537205-robert">Robert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780061976261" href="/book/show/6948234-sandman-slim">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5537205-robert?shelf=robert-s-reads">robert-s-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5537205-robert?shelf=left-coast-crime">left-coast-crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer978725684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5720519741392616209">If our personalities are derived from the characters and novels we tend to enjoy (in my case both reading and writing), then I’d make a strong candidate for <b>Shithead of the Year.</b> Hell, I don’t even need a running mate. I suppose I could leave it at that, and just walk away, probably leaving more than a few of you scratching your heads. But I might as well expound upon my point, because once you start shoveling shit you might as well keep going.<br/><br/>You see, James Stark is a character I’m not supposed</span>
  <span id="freeText5720519741392616209" style="display:none">If our personalities are derived from the characters and novels we tend to enjoy (in my case both reading and writing), then I’d make a strong candidate for <b>Shithead of the Year.</b> Hell, I don’t even need a running mate. I suppose I could leave it at that, and just walk away, probably leaving more than a few of you scratching your heads. But I might as well expound upon my point, because once you start shoveling shit you might as well keep going.<br /><br />You see, James Stark is a character I’m not supposed to like. In fact, he burns jackets, kills people (bad ones), and even manages to piss off a few angels just for fun. He’s the kind of guy you’re better off pretending you don’t know. If he does happen to come around, you barricade your front door, and then you call the fuzz. If the cops can’t keep him at bay, then you leave LA (it’s filled with people more fucked up than Stark anyway), and head somewhere safer like Mexico or Colombia.<br /><br />Despite all of that, though, I actually liked the bastard. I rooted for him to rein hell-on-earth and kick the shit out of evil, and ruin a few more coats. I could almost feel his hatred coursing through my veins, and rather than be turned off, I was actually a little turned on. To be fair, it wasn’t all fireflies and sparklers, and I did manage to cringe once or twice, based on yet another terrible path he took. But if I didn’t see at least a fault or two, I’d probably be in more trouble than I already am. So maybe there’s the slimmest of slim chances I’m not completely fucked up.<br /><br />In the spirit of Stark smashing a few faces, SANDMAN SLIM smashed together more than one genre, and made it work. The plot and dialogue raced forward (other than enough editing errors that I couldn’t help but notice); all the characters were filled with warm and gooey goodness (smirks); the action made it seem as though I was driving on two-wheels down Wilshire Boulevard (without traffic); and I even discovered another reason to hate a junkie or two (when you read it, you’ll see what I mean).<br /><br />Like this novel so aptly proves time and again: <i>What doesn’t kill you makes you stronger.</i><br /><br />I received this book for free at Left Coast Crime.<br /><br /><a href="http://www.robertdowns.net/blog/" rel="nofollow noopener">Cross-posted at Robert's Reads</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5720519741392616209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1646406191" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1646406191" />
    <a title="Pippa DaCosta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23314834-pippa-dacosta"><img alt="Pippa DaCosta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499153245p2/23314834.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1646406191?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pippa DaCosta" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pippa DaCosta" href="/user/show/23314834-pippa-dacosta">Pippa DaCosta</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23314834-pippa-dacosta?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23314834-pippa-dacosta?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23314834-pippa-dacosta?shelf=tough-guy-urban-fantasy">tough-guy-urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1646406191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14378613390510278261"><b>This is crazy, dirty urban fantasy at its most deliciously brutal. </b><br/><br/>Stark (don’t call him Jimmy) is back from Hell, and he’s got a one track mind. All he wants is to kill the people who put him <i>Downtown</i> 11 years ago, and killed his girl. Save the world? Hell no. Be a hero? F*ck that. He boosts cars like most people catch busses, smokes like a train, and has a knack for not dying. And he really doesn’t give a shit for anything or anyone—only his revenge. <br/><br/>While he’s getting his revenge, people keep</span>
  <span id="freeText14378613390510278261" style="display:none"><b>This is crazy, dirty urban fantasy at its most deliciously brutal. </b><br><br>Stark (don’t call him Jimmy) is back from Hell, and he’s got a one track mind. All he wants is to kill the people who put him <i>Downtown</i> 11 years ago, and killed his girl. Save the world? Hell no. Be a hero? F*ck that. He boosts cars like most people catch busses, smokes like a train, and has a knack for not dying. And he really doesn’t give a shit for anything or anyone—only his revenge. <br><br>While he’s getting his revenge, people keep getting in his way. Some want to hire him, some die as collateral damage, most just want <i>him</i> dead. That’s their problem. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467111967ra/19553009.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He’s a monster, he knows it, and he embraces it. <br><br>The first person present tense doesn’t pull any punches. It’s all up in your face getting angsty like a crackhead needing his next fix. No chapters, just scene breaks, means this is one non-stop action-packed page-turner. And to think I almost didn’t read it?! I’m not a big fan of first person present, and when I opened it up to find the writing style immediately kicking me in the face, I almost put it to one side for good. But, I tried again, gave it a few pages, and <i>bam</i>, I was sucked right in. <br><br>We have angels, anti-angels, vampires (jades), demons (of course), and a whole bunch of other bad-ass mofo’s from the supernatural crew. A magic coin that swears like a sailor, the undead head of a video rentals dude, kick-ass Candy—so much urban fantasy goodness. Honestly, it’s a spine-ripping, gut-punching, thrill ride. <br><br>The warning on the back has it right. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467111967i/19553010._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can’t wait to get my teeth into the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14378613390510278261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
