<div id="review_2715294963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2715294963" />
    <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader"><img alt="Heidi The Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593309467p2/7986781.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2715294963?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi The Reader" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader">Heidi The Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fantasy-and-sci-fi">fantasy-and-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2715294963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3644622971356460029"><i>Sandman Slim</i> is a dark, urban fantasy read about a magician who was given to demons by people he considered his friends. Now, James Stark's back for revenge.<br/><br/>Because, what does he have to lose. He's already been to hell.<br/><br/><i>".. I'm lucky that way. Always have been. Otherwise, I might have crawled back into this world and ended up a charcoal briquette in my first five minutes home. And wouldn't those black-hearted bastards down under have laughed when I ended right back in Hell after slipping so sweet</i></span>
  <span id="freeText3644622971356460029" style="display:none"><i>Sandman Slim</i> is a dark, urban fantasy read about a magician who was given to demons by people he considered his friends. Now, James Stark's back for revenge.<br /><br />Because, what does he have to lose. He's already been to hell.<br /><br /><i>".. I'm lucky that way. Always have been. Otherwise, I might have crawled back into this world and ended up a charcoal briquette in my first five minutes home. And wouldn't those black-hearted bastards down under have laughed when I ended right back in Hell after slipping so sweetly out the back door?</i> pgs 1-2<br /><br />James is not just claiming revenge for himself. While he was with the demons, someone killed the love of his life. That someone is going to have to pay.<br /><br /><i>I've been gone eleven years. I was nineteen when I went Downtown. I'm practically an old man now.</i> pgs 11-12<br /><br />Meanwhile on earth, someone or something has been causing more chaos and destruction than usual. Los Angeles, though never particularly a "city of angels", seems to be something much worse now. But why should James care — he's not going to be around long enough to figure out what's going on anyway.<br /><br />I really enjoyed <i>Sandman Slim</i>. James Stark is brooding, angry and you can't help but hope for him to succeed.<br /><br /><i>Revenge is never what you think it's going to be. There's no pleasure or glory, and when you're done your grief remains.</i> pg 54<br /><br />The world Richard Kadrey has created has levels and different forms of spirituality and magic. Angels, demons and monsters walk the streets, in plain view but hidden from those who don't know what they're looking at.<br /><br />There's an alchemist named Vidocq who accidentally made himself immortal. A mysterious doctor who helps those in the magical community but doesn't charge for his services. And readers are also introduced to Allegra, a beautiful young woman who runs a video shop and wants to learn more about magic.<br /><br /><i>"Where was God when I was stuck in Hell?" I ask her. .... "Maybe God thought you were where you belonged.</i> pg 228<br /><br />Recommended for readers who don't mind their urban fantasy reads filled with some profanity and angry heroes.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1586558932" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1586558932" />
    <a title="Scott Sigler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1782315-scott-sigler"><img alt="Scott Sigler" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442455917p2/1782315.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1586558932?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott Sigler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott Sigler" href="/user/show/1782315-scott-sigler">Scott Sigler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1586558932" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17851005452421534762">A kick-ass book. <br/><br/>It's DRESDEN FILES meets DEXTER meets DIRTY HARRY. Foul-mouthed and bad-tempered to the gills.<br/><br/>You can see the DEXTER influence in this concept. Instead of a "serial killer who kills serial killers," you have a "monster that kills monsters." That was one of the few angles of this book that didn't work for me, though, as the main character is human an a "monster" only in spirit. <br/><br/>Kadrey has a gift for PULP FICTION-esque dialogue, rapid-fire and full of creative insults. <br/><br/>This is boo</span>
  <span id="freeText17851005452421534762" style="display:none">A kick-ass book. <br /><br />It's DRESDEN FILES meets DEXTER meets DIRTY HARRY. Foul-mouthed and bad-tempered to the gills.<br /><br />You can see the DEXTER influence in this concept. Instead of a "serial killer who kills serial killers," you have a "monster that kills monsters." That was one of the few angles of this book that didn't work for me, though, as the main character is human an a "monster" only in spirit. <br /><br />Kadrey has a gift for PULP FICTION-esque dialogue, rapid-fire and full of creative insults. <br /><br />This is book one of a series that seems destined to follow the Sookie Steakhouse / Harry Dresden / Buffy Summers route of one Big Bad after another, all slightly escalating the stakes, as each subsequent tale builds to the <em>ultimate</em> big bad somewhere down the road. <br /><br />If you are a fan of supernatural stories, two-fisted tales, anti-heroes and/or copious amounts of hard liquor, you'll probably enjoy this book. </span>

<div id="review_284016272" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/284016272" />
    <a title="AH" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3255548-ah"><img alt="AH" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275413869p2/3255548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/284016272?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AH" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AH" href="/user/show/3255548-ah">AH</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780061999444" href="/book/show/7598206-sandman-slim">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=kobo-freebies">kobo-freebies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=sos-bookshelf-bingo">sos-bookshelf-bingo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=babr-reviews">babr-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=angels">angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=zzread-feb-2012">zzread-feb-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer284016272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8849889930869230888">Sandman Slim is the story of James Stark. Stark has quite a chip on his shoulder: He was sent to Hell at age 19 and has languished there for 11 years. Stark is out for revenge and wants to kill those responsible for his time “Downtown.”<br/><br/>Told from Stark’s point of view, the narrative voice combines a wicked sense of humor with irreverence, snark, and the need to get even with those who wronged him. Stark is a complex character: He is still grieving the death of his first love Alice. At the same ti</span>
  <span id="freeText8849889930869230888" style="display:none">Sandman Slim is the story of James Stark. Stark has quite a chip on his shoulder: He was sent to Hell at age 19 and has languished there for 11 years. Stark is out for revenge and wants to kill those responsible for his time “Downtown.”<br /><br />Told from Stark’s point of view, the narrative voice combines a wicked sense of humor with irreverence, snark, and the need to get even with those who wronged him. Stark is a complex character: He is still grieving the death of his first love Alice. At the same time, there doesn’t seem to be a car in L.A. that cannot be hotwired by Stark. Stark is adept at all kinds of weapons use. He is also a magician, but he hesitates to use his magic for fear of attracting the attention of the Hellions. Stark is also difficult to kill, a definite asset in his world. <br /><br />The world building is quite extensive and the use of L.A. and its’ seedy side adds a dark, urban feel to this book. Stark’s memories of his time in Hell and his descriptions of the various factions at war there add color and texture to the narrative. <br /><br />I was also impressed by the variety of different paranormal creatures. While there were the usual angels, demons, and vampires, there were also the Kissi – a freaky kind of fallen angel. One of my favorite characters was a Jade – a kind of vampire with shark teeth. <br /><br />The eclectic mix of characters makes this book very interesting. I loved Vidocq, Stark’s old friend and companion. Allegra, the Goth video store clerk was a surprising character. Candy the Jade was a perfect partner for Stark. <br /><br />The story is well paced and there are some fantastic action sequences that kept me on the edge of my seat. Stark and his friends like their guns and know how to use them. My only criticism of this book is that there were absolutely no chapter breaks. I never really could tell where I could stop and take a break. Not a big problem; I finished the book fairly quickly. <br /><br />Favorite quotes<br /><i></i><p>“Now you are thinking like a thief. Fewer guns and more exits. We’ll cure your cowboy ways yet.”</p><p>“We’re monkeys in trees one day and the next we’re monkeys with dental hygiene and cell phones. Best of all, we don’t throw shit at each other anymore.”</p><br /><b>Review posted on <a href="http://badassbookreviews.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Badass Book Reviews</a></b>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8849889930869230888" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_863081037" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/863081037" />
    <a title="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books"><img alt="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415550632p2/5892196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/863081037?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" href="/user/show/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books">Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/18170815-sandman-slim">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=own-digital-audiobook">own-digital-audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=own-kindle-copy">own-kindle-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer863081037" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2687839727344885429">This review can also be found at <a href='https://carolesrandomlife.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carole's Random Life in Books</a>.<br/><br/>I feel like I have been wanting to read this book forever. I bought the ebook more than eight years ago and added the audiobook to my collection nearly six years ago. I am not really sure why it took me so long to finally get started with the series but I am happy to report that this book is really as good as I had hoped it would be. I am so glad that I finally took the time to give this one a listen.<br/><br/>James Stark was only 19 years old</span>
  <span id="freeText2687839727344885429" style="display:none">This review can also be found at <a href="https://carolesrandomlife.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Carole's Random Life in Books</a>.<br /><br />I feel like I have been wanting to read this book forever. I bought the ebook more than eight years ago and added the audiobook to my collection nearly six years ago. I am not really sure why it took me so long to finally get started with the series but I am happy to report that this book is really as good as I had hoped it would be. I am so glad that I finally took the time to give this one a listen.<br /><br />James Stark was only 19 years old when he went to Hell. It is now 11 years later and he is back and ready to deal with the friends who sent him away. The past 11 years have been hard on Stark but he survived and picked up a few skills along the way. Things have changed in the world while he was away and he has a few adjustments to make as he works to settle the score.<br /><br />I really liked Stark. He is tough and able to think on his feet. We learn pretty early on that he can be rather brutal when necessary but he will also go out of his way to help others who are truly innocent. We really learn a lot about Stark in this book and I think that his past and time in Hell have helped to shape him. Stark does have a sense of humor and there were times that I found myself chuckling. I also really enjoyed the supporting cast of characters and I think that the whole ensemble really helped to make the story entertaining.<br /><br />This story is really exciting. It is really interesting right out of the gate and everything builds as the story progresses. I like that there is no big information dump as you sometimes find in the first installment in a series. Instead, the world-building happens slowly as the story is told. There is plenty of action to keep things moving and a few scenes where we really get to see how much Stark has lost. I think that the pacing of the story was very well done and I liked that I was always eager to get back to the story.<br /><br />MacLeod Andrews did a phenomenal job with the narration of this book. He really brought James Stark to life and I couldn't imagine this character having a different voice. He handled all of the character voices extremely well and added a lot of excitement to the story. I know that I enjoyed this story a bit more because of his narration.<br /><br />I would not hesitate to recommend this book to others. This is a very strong start to a series that I can't wait to continue. The characters were very well done and I found myself completely engaged in the story from beginning to end. I cannot wait to read more of this series!<br /><br /><b>Initial Thoughts</b><br />I ended up really enjoying this one. The narrator of the audiobook does an amazing job with this story and the story itself is really exciting. Stark is a great character. The more that we learned about him, the more I found that I liked him. There is a lot going on in this story and I found that I had to start the audiobook over at the midpoint since I was pretty sure I missed some key points. It was worth putting in that extra time. I like that there was a bit of humor that was worked into this story along with some pretty intense action. I cannot wait to read more of Stark and the rest of the gang.<br /><br />Book source: purchase</span>
  <a data-text-id="2687839727344885429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_718403451" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/718403451" />
    <a title="Benji Glaab" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19373934-benji-glaab"><img alt="Benji Glaab" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538708163p2/19373934.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/718403451?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benji Glaab" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benji Glaab" href="/user/show/19373934-benji-glaab">Benji Glaab</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer718403451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer796331631420601978">After doing an 11 year tour in hell honing his skills at killing and practically having a threesome with pain and suffering, James Stark has returned to a scum infested L.A.<br/><br/><br/>Seeking revenge on ex-friends that were at the center of the scheming betrayel that sent Jimmy on a trip "downtown". Sandman slim could live with that, however wrought with guilt for not being able to protect his only love he's intent on tracking down the man responsible for her death, Mason the plots mastermind and talented </span>
  <span id="freeText796331631420601978" style="display:none">After doing an 11 year tour in hell honing his skills at killing and practically having a threesome with pain and suffering, James Stark has returned to a scum infested L.A.<br /><br /><br />Seeking revenge on ex-friends that were at the center of the scheming betrayel that sent Jimmy on a trip "downtown". Sandman slim could live with that, however wrought with guilt for not being able to protect his only love he's intent on tracking down the man responsible for her death, Mason the plots mastermind and talented magician. <br /><br /><br />This book made for an exceptional quick read. Filled to the rim with action packed laughs along the way. I loved Kadrey's voice throughout the tale. He speaks to an average audience. Although clever there's nothing fancy about his delivery. Perfect style for this type of story.<br /><br /><br /><br />I love Sandman slim's introspection. It didn't give me too much to think about , but did it ever give me a great sense for what kind of character he truly is.<br /><br /><br /><br /> What's to like<br /><br /><br />Sandman's arsenal was off the chain. He has Old west dusters, sawed off shotguns, Some Hellion specialties Azazeal's Blade which doubles as a key that can unlock virtually anything, and my personal fave A Na'at <br />"Traditionally you use a na'at like a spear or a staff, but there's another trigger that collapse the central shaft. Suddenly the na'at is as loose as chicken chow mein, a metal whip that can strip the skin off a rhino like peeling a grape. Not that I've ever peeled a rhino or a grape, but you get the idea."<br /> Combine some cool weapons with handy earth magic, and Hellion Hexes and you've got a magician killing machine.<br /><br /><br /><br /> Sandman slim's favorite pass times<br /><br /><br />- Grand theft auto, he Jacks at least 2-3 vehicles daily.<br /><br />- Watching movies most people haven't heard of.<br /><br />- Smoking, drinking jack Daniels, And making out with mega babe monster chicks that on occasion drink people.<br /><br /><br />Needless to say Kadrey had a lot of fun creating the sandman slim character. And this translated throughout the entire story to me the reader.<br /><br /> Final thoughts<br /><br />Let it be known I love the crazed vigilante Frank Castle. I figure if the Punisher went to hell and came back we'd be looking at Sandman slim. I feel Kadrey payed homage to the genre. and I wouldn't be the least bit surprised to learn that Kadrey was inspired by some great graphic novels like Neil Gaiman's Sandman<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23754.Preludes___Nocturnes__The_Sandman___1_" title="Preludes &amp; Nocturnes (The Sandman, #1) by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sandman, Vol. 1: Preludes and Nocturnes</a>, well duh it's just the hell aspect was structured with many similarities. Also Hellblazer <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/133017.Hellblazer_Original_Sins" title="Hellblazer Original Sins by Jamie Delano" rel="nofollow noopener">Hellblazer: Original Sins</a> James Stark's back story totally reminded me of John Constantine.<br /><br />I would recommend this book for anyone who likes action quick paced (people that play video games) anyone that's dabbled in 90's era graphic novels. Or anyone that's stuck in a reading rut looking to try something fun with a little quirk.</span>
  <a data-text-id="796331631420601978" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_473139450" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/473139450" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/473139450?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780061999444" href="/book/show/7598206-sandman-slim">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer473139450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4529815408934324525">I don't normally like urban fantasy, nor do I care much for anything involving Heaven, Hell, or any of the mythical beasts roaming around those lands. The difference here is Richard Kadrey's writing. His prose is faster than a bullet and as vulgar as a sailor pounding the back door out of a two dollar lady of the night. If that last sentence offended you, please stay away from Sandman Slim. The main character's first-person narration is far more blue. If you like crass descriptions and foul-mout</span>
  <span id="freeText4529815408934324525" style="display:none">I don't normally like urban fantasy, nor do I care much for anything involving Heaven, Hell, or any of the mythical beasts roaming around those lands. The difference here is Richard Kadrey's writing. His prose is faster than a bullet and as vulgar as a sailor pounding the back door out of a two dollar lady of the night. If that last sentence offended you, please stay away from Sandman Slim. The main character's first-person narration is far more blue. If you like crass descriptions and foul-mouth anecdotes, Sandman Slim is stuffed full of hilarity and offensive charm.<br /><br />Another reason I should have hated this book is the present tense storytelling, but once again, Richard pulled it off. I normally put down a book as soon as I see the first "is" instead of "was," because I don't feel present tense is believable. I mean, how is the story being related? The only present tense stuff I can stand is normally short fiction and blog posts. I constantly wonder whether or not the narrator has a voice recorder in his pocket. If your doing this right now, how the hell are you writing it. I know, I know, I'm being to damn literal, but that's how I feel. I have no idea why I was able to withstand the tense of this book and not others. I just did. <br /><br />I loved the fact that the main character, James Stark, (aka Sandman Slim) doesn't care about anything else aside from his own revenge. The world is going to end, and the only reason he's saves it is because the person bringing about hell on earth is the guy who killed his girlfriend. It's a very human story surrounded by magic and supernatural evils. Not to mention, one fun ride. <br /><br />For those of you that care about typos and grammatical foibles, I will say that the book is full of words left in after editing, missing words and several instances where "bought" is used instead of "brought." I could almost see someone using the find function in word and accidentally replacing every instance with the wrong word. Oh, and for the ebook version, there are several formatting issues. Mostly with the dialogue. One person will talk and the quotation marks will close out the speech, but then another piece of dialogue, from a completely different person, will start up without a new paragraph. Nobody's perfect, not even the Big Six guys. But most of you already know that. The only reason I even mention it is because I know some of you will care enough to stop reading, which, in my opinion, would be a grand mistake, indeed.<br /><br />I will definitely be checking out the rest of the Sandman Slim series.<br /><br />E.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4529815408934324525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_69223206" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/69223206" />
    <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon"><img alt="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572581488p2/1209800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/69223206?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon">colleen the convivial curmudgeon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780061999444" href="/book/show/7598206-sandman-slim">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=horror-esque">horror-esque</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=library-read">library-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=group-read">group-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69223206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer172177769531765964">So, this book is a basic "back for revenge" kind of thing. Our protagonist gets sent bodily to hell, somehow manages to survive for 11 years, then gets embedded with a magic key that lets him go anywhere, and comes back for revenge after they kill his girl.<br/><br/>There are some interesting concepts - a bit of a twist that the guy coming back from Hell is still actually alive, some cool weaponry, like the na'at which is a weapon from Hell which is pretty mutatable, some magical stuff, so on and so forth</span>
  <span id="freeText172177769531765964" style="display:none">So, this book is a basic "back for revenge" kind of thing. Our protagonist gets sent bodily to hell, somehow manages to survive for 11 years, then gets embedded with a magic key that lets him go anywhere, and comes back for revenge after they kill his girl.<br /><br />There are some interesting concepts - a bit of a twist that the guy coming back from Hell is still actually alive, some cool weaponry, like the na'at which is a weapon from Hell which is pretty mutatable, some magical stuff, so on and so forth.<br /><br />But the writing's pretty terrible. I mean, even for a pulp book. It was very jumpy. More than once I wondered if I was missing a page or a chapter or something, because he'd be cleaning up bodies, and then thinking of gum. (Ok, not a real example, but you get the general idea.)<br /><br />And he's pretty one-note - all of the characters are - and he's constantly flying off half-cocked and doing stupid things and getting other people hurt and just generally being a ponce. (The author makes some nods at trying to explain some of this. He time in Hell gave him impulse control problems, for instance, but it was pretty damn annoying to read about it over and over and over again.)<br /><br />All in all, it wasn't terrible and I wouldn't say "Oh dear gods, no, don't read this book!", but I'm less than motivated to read any more of it (especially since I've heard the sequel's "not as good" as the first.)<br /><br />In a way it's unfortunate because the last third of the book, after the rather anti-climactic big battle, the things that were there to sort of set-up the continuation actually started getting somewhat more interesting. Not enough, though, for me to check it out.<br /><br /><br />I do think it had some interesting concepts and characters, though, especially if they're developed a bit more, but I think it could work much better as a movie or as a comic because the narration is really the worst part of the whole thing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="172177769531765964" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_136169493" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136169493" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/136169493?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136169493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14486141955580072467">Remember that movie The Crow, with Brandon Lee? Ok. Sandman Slim has that same vibe...minus the emo goth-boy hero and scruffy little girl with a skateboard.<br/><br/>James Stark is the pulp fiction style anti-hero of this story, who has literally been to Hell and back. <br/>Eleven years after being betrayed by a group of magicians, whose leader used Stark as the sacrifice to catapult himself to incredible power, he escapes from Hell with a new name and a new reputation. <i>Sandman Slim</i>, the monster who kills mons</span>
  <span id="freeText14486141955580072467" style="display:none">Remember that movie The Crow, with Brandon Lee? Ok. Sandman Slim has that same vibe...minus the emo goth-boy hero and scruffy little girl with a skateboard.<br /><br />James Stark is the pulp fiction style anti-hero of this story, who has literally been to Hell and back. <br />Eleven years after being betrayed by a group of magicians, whose leader used Stark as the sacrifice to catapult himself to incredible power, he escapes from Hell with a new name and a new reputation. <i>Sandman Slim</i>, the monster who kills monsters. As the only living human in Hell, he was quite a novelty, and <i>not</i> in a good way. And now that he's back, it's time for a little payback. <br /><br />This book isn't for everyone, but if you enjoy dark and dirty, you'll like this. It's not a perfect book, and there were a few times I found myself thinking, <i>why'd he do <b>that</b>, when he could have done <b>this</b>?</i>, or <i>WTF is up with all of his <b>names</b></i>. Overall, though, this book was just a lot of fun. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14486141955580072467" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1736749921" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1736749921" />
    <a title="Ariel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22465719-ariel"><img alt="Ariel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508179437p2/22465719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1736749921?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ariel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ariel" href="/user/show/22465719-ariel">Ariel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/12470865-sandman-slim">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22465719-ariel?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22465719-ariel?shelf=paranormal-supernatural">paranormal-supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22465719-ariel?shelf=would-recommend">would-recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22465719-ariel?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22465719-ariel?shelf=dark-morbid">dark-morbid</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22465719-ariel?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22465719-ariel?shelf=audible-account">audible-account</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22465719-ariel?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1736749921" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3827697266682326657"><b>"Don't be modest, we've all heard of you. Sandman Slim-the monster who kills monsters."</b><br/><br/>In an effort to regain control over my TBR and my Audible account, I made an excellent executive decision to re-listen to <b>Sandman Slim</b> and I think I enjoyed myself so much more this second time around.<br/><br/>Richard Stark is the anti-hero of all anti-heroes, a self-centered jackass of a magician sent to hell by his magicians circle in exchange for all sorts of excellent power. Instead of dying, which is what everyone</span>
  <span id="freeText3827697266682326657" style="display:none"><b>"Don't be modest, we've all heard of you. Sandman Slim-the monster who kills monsters."</b><br /><br />In an effort to regain control over my TBR and my Audible account, I made an excellent executive decision to re-listen to <b>Sandman Slim</b> and I think I enjoyed myself so much more this second time around.<br /><br />Richard Stark is the anti-hero of all anti-heroes, a self-centered jackass of a magician sent to hell by his magicians circle in exchange for all sorts of excellent power. Instead of dying, which is what everyone, including the denizens and generals of hell and hell's army expected, Stark was thrown into the Pits to fight the monsters of hell, Gladiator style. Eleven years of fighting demons and darkness can do a number on a person and it reflects in Stark when he's able to drag his smoking ass up and claw his way back to the the world.<br /><br />This guy is a total asshole. He's unfriendly, rude, focused on his mission of revenge and vengeance and has no room in his life for anything but smokes and booze. But honestly, don't let that fool you, because Stark is definitely one of those truffles that has the hidden ooey, gooey center that tries to hide that fact. He's a fabulous jerkwad and I adore his grinchy little heart.<br /><br />Richard Kadrey created a fabulous pulp-fiction noir seedy underbelly anti-hero goodness. It's over the top in the best ways, with some humor that had me literally giggling out loud. My husband, who only knows that this "Supernatural the TV show on roids", overheard me listening to this for about a minute long and laughed out loud as well. He had no idea what was happening or who was who, he just knew the goodness of raunchy humor and sailor talk.<br /><br />I'll also be honest and admit I love a good "good vs. evil" battle. Angels and demons fighting for the control of humanity and the universe is always a good read because I feel each writer really does put their own individual spin on it, and I really enjoyed Kadrey's. <br /><br />This world building and story telling is unique and interesting and keeps me entertained above all. The narrator, GOD BLESS YOU MACLEOD ANDREWS, your voice is cigarettes, gravel and whiskey all rolled into one. Literally one of the best narrators because he just FITS Stark so well! The narration for the other voices and cast of character is also top notch and very well done. I really enjoy the hesitancy that's projected into Candy and the over the top Texan accent for the non-Texan Wells. Plus, they do some great audio work in overlapping voices when demons are involved and it really adds to the atmosphere.<br /><br />The only downside to audio as a medium is that I'm not quite sure on the correct spelling for quite a few of the characters, and I'd really rather not go hunting down for names. I will say that everyone you are introduced to is interesting and adds to the story. There are no side characters that are added for us additions sake, but everyone is important to the story. <br /><br />I highly recommend <b>Sandman Slim</b> to anyone that is either in the mood for a laugh, or is looking to try something new in a genre they haven't read before. This is a great urban fantasy with pulp-noir overtones and a side of comedy and irreverent humor that will get you giggling against your will. I also highly recommend giving this a shot as audiobook as the narration is just fantastic and adds so well to the story.<br /><br />To close my review, I leave you with one of the last and most beautiful words said by Stark that I can relate to so well.<br /><b>"Fuck me, I'm a rock star and all I wanted was a burrito."</b> Amen, Stark, amen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3827697266682326657" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_489850355" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/489850355" />
    <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc"><img alt="Mogsy (MMOGC)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286325553p2/4379514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/489850355?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mogsy (MMOGC)" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc">Mogsy (MMOGC)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=urban">urban</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=religion">religion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=angels-and-demons">angels-and-demons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer489850355" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14808505706870729974">Whoa, this was dark. And also fun. It's got that whole "I don't give a fuck" attitude emanating off of it in droves, and you know what? I actually kinda liked that. <br/><br/>I've read more urban fantasy in the recent months than I have in years. I like the genre; I admit it's grown on me. But sometimes, I just need an urban fantasy fix that doesn't involve any messy paranormal romances with werewolves, vampires, or faeries, you know what I mean? Sandman Slim was the perfect break from that, with its grit</span>
  <span id="freeText14808505706870729974" style="display:none">Whoa, this was dark. And also fun. It's got that whole "I don't give a fuck" attitude emanating off of it in droves, and you know what? I actually kinda liked that. <br /><br />I've read more urban fantasy in the recent months than I have in years. I like the genre; I admit it's grown on me. But sometimes, I just need an urban fantasy fix that doesn't involve any messy paranormal romances with werewolves, vampires, or faeries, you know what I mean? Sandman Slim was the perfect break from that, with its gritty story about demons and fallen angels and a main character who, like in most urban fantasy books starring a male protagonist, is hilarious and always armed with a treasure trove of pop culture references and creative metaphors. <br /><br />Stark is also so angsty and full of rage that I'm actually kind of worried if I'd be able to take it if he remains this curmudgeon-y for the rest of the series. I am still picking up the next book though, no doubt about it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14808505706870729974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IFkcIzRhKuEx32cotV+VLTgSlvteRNkHVPOHPB7/3ErQ3OCZYahL5D8yIzEt+clnPtkw7mbZ427evQGvzkcggw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
